          --monorail-metadata-toggled-bg: var(--monorail-metadata-closed-bg);
        }
        mr-issue-page[codeFont] {
          --mr-toggled-font-family: Monospace;
        }
        .container-issue {
          width: 100%;
          flex-direction: column;
          align-items: stretch;
          justify-content: flex-start;
          z-index: 200;
        }

          margin: auto;
          padding: 0;

          flex-direction: row;
          flex-wrap: no-wrap;
        }

        }

          flex-grow: 0;

        }

          width: 100%;

          padding-right: var(--mr-issue-page-horizontal-padding);

          overflow-y: auto;

          height: calc(100vh - var(--monorail-header-height));
        }

          }
          mr-issue-details, mr-launch-overview {
            width: 100%;

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>

        <p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

        <h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>

        <p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>

        <p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

Another bug is that we can add more than one (dot) in accept extension: ['.jpg.bat']. but why?



<span class="line"><!---->Another bug is that we can add more than one (dot) in accept extension: ['.jpg.bat']. but why?<!----></span>



<br>





It allows the website developer to add characters to the filename. If a user has hidden file extensions (default option on Windows) He will see more legit virus filename (picture1)



<span class="line"><!---->It allows the website developer to add characters to the filename. If a user has hidden file extensions (default option on Windows) He will see more legit virus filename (picture1)<!----></span>



<br>





Solution: Only one dot in accept extension.



<span class="line"><!---->Solution: Only one dot in accept extension.<!----></span>

In documentation there is:



<span class="line"><!---->In documentation there is:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





https://wicg.github.io/file-system-access/#security-malware



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://wicg.github.io/file-system-access/#security-malware"><!---->https://wicg.github.io/file-system-access/#security-malware<!----></a>



<br>



<br>





"This API could be used by websites to try to store and/or execute malware on the users system.



<span class="line"><!---->"This API could be used by websites to try to store and/or execute malware on the users system.<!----></span>



<br>





To mitigate this risk, this API does not provide any way to mark files as executable



<span class="line"><!---->To mitigate this risk, this API does not provide any way to mark files as executable<!----></span>



<br>





(on the other hand files that are already executable likely remain that way, even after the files are modified through this API)"



<span class="line"><!---->(on the other hand files that are already executable likely remain that way, even after the files are modified through this API)"<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





"not provide any way to mark files as executable" - I can save executable .bat and spoof as an .jpg. I can mark it to save as .bat??? So it is not working as planned.



<span class="line"><!---->"not provide any way to mark files as executable" - I can save executable .bat and spoof as an .jpg. I can mark it to save as .bat??? So it is not working as planned.<!----></span>



<br>





I am a bit confused here. :P



<span class="line"><!---->I am a bit confused here. :P<!----></span>

Another bug. If user has option "show all file extensions." activated, we can hide real extension by adding many white chars to accept extension. 



<span class="line"><!---->Another bug. If user has option "show all file extensions." activated, we can hide real extension by adding many white chars to accept extension. <!----></span>



<br>





Solution: Accept extension shouldn't allow many white spaces. Should be limited with max chars or array of legit chars excluding white chars.



<span class="line"><!---->Solution: Accept extension shouldn't allow many white spaces. Should be limited with max chars or array of legit chars excluding white chars.<!----></span>

Now I have understood the mechanism of description variable



<span class="line"><!---->Now I have understood the mechanism of description variable<!----></span>



<br>





description = "JPEG (.jpeg)" then in download window we can see: "JPEG (.jpeg) (*.exe;*.txt;*.text)" (picture10.png) - works good! Chrome is adding real extensions.



<span class="line"><!---->description = "JPEG (.jpeg)" then in download window we can see: "JPEG (.jpeg) (*.exe;*.txt;*.text)" (picture10.png) - works good! Chrome is adding real extensions.<!----></span>



<br>





However we can bypass this in 2 ways:



<span class="line"><!---->However we can bypass this in 2 ways:<!----></span>



<br>





1 method: Add extra space to description:



<span class="line"><!---->1 method: Add extra space to description:<!----></span>



<br>





description = "JPEG (.jpeg)                       (50+more white chars)" then in download window we can see: "JPEG (.jpeg)" (picture11.png)



<span class="line"><!---->description = "JPEG (.jpeg)                       (50+more white chars)" then in download window we can see: "JPEG (.jpeg)" (picture11.png)<!----></span>



<br>





2 method: Add *. to description:



<span class="line"><!---->2 method: Add *. to description:<!----></span>



<br>





description = "JPEG (*.jpeg)" then in download window we can see: "JPEG (*.jpeg)" (picture12.png)



<span class="line"><!---->description = "JPEG (*.jpeg)" then in download window we can see: "JPEG (*.jpeg)" (picture12.png)<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Solution: Always add real extensions. Block * character and multiple white characters.



<span class="line"><!---->Solution: Always add real extensions. Block * character and multiple white characters.<!----></span>







<mr-comment-content></mr-comment-content>


        


          




            




      


        


          




          



picture10.png



<b><!---->picture10.png<!----></b>


          




        

<div class="filename">
          
          <b><!---->picture10.png<!----></b>
          
        </div>


        


          


            



4.0 KB

NEXT SECURITY vulnerability:



<span class="line"><!---->NEXT SECURITY vulnerability:<!----></span>



<br>





Based on default/main download function:



<span class="line"><!---->Based on default/main download function:<!----></span>



<br>





showSaveFilePicker bypassing the function "IsShellIntegratedExtension": 



<span class="line"><!---->showSaveFilePicker bypassing the function "IsShellIntegratedExtension": <!----></span>





https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/master:net/base/filename_util_internal.cc;drc=1c58af32060fa0ef3cfd4037fdc7913092d16ba2;l=155?q=%20EnsureSafeExtension&ss=chromium



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/master:net/base/filename_util_internal.cc;drc=1c58af32060fa0ef3cfd4037fdc7913092d16ba2;l=155?q=%20EnsureSafeExtension&amp;ss=chromium"><!---->https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/master:net/base/filename_util_internal.cc;drc=1c58af32060fa0ef3cfd4037fdc7913092d16ba2;l=155?q=%20EnsureSafeExtension&amp;ss=chromium<!----></a>



<br>





if extension ".lnk" or ".local" then Chrome should CHANGE extension to ".download", but not doing this:



<span class="line"><!---->if extension ".lnk" or ".local" then Chrome should CHANGE extension to ".download", but not doing this:<!----></span>



<br>





https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/master:net/base/filename_util_internal.cc;drc=1c58af32060fa0ef3cfd4037fdc7913092d16ba2;l=195?q=%20EnsureSafeExtension&ss=chromium



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/master:net/base/filename_util_internal.cc;drc=1c58af32060fa0ef3cfd4037fdc7913092d16ba2;l=195?q=%20EnsureSafeExtension&amp;ss=chromium"><!---->https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/master:net/base/filename_util_internal.cc;drc=1c58af32060fa0ef3cfd4037fdc7913092d16ba2;l=195?q=%20EnsureSafeExtension&amp;ss=chromium<!----></a>



<br>





Solution: Replace ".lnk" and ".local" with ".download" or block downloading such a file.



<span class="line"><!---->Solution: Replace ".lnk" and ".local" with ".download" or block downloading such a file.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





URL EXAMPLE: 



<span class="line"><!---->URL EXAMPLE: <!----></span>





https://nfz.dev/lnk.html



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://nfz.dev/lnk.html"><!---->https://nfz.dev/lnk.html<!----></a>

Would you mind filing separate bugs for separate issues? That will make it easier to track work fixing/triaging them, and make sure they don't fall through the gaps.



<span class="line"><!---->Would you mind filing separate bugs for separate issues? That will make it easier to track work fixing/triaging them, and make sure they don't fall through the gaps.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Re 



<span class="line"><!---->Re <!----></span>





comment #4



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="#c4"><!---->comment #4<!----></a>





, supporting dots in extensions (i.e. "compound extensions") is something that we do need to support, as some file types do use that. For example things like .tar.gz. See also 



<span class="line"><!---->, supporting dots in extensions (i.e. "compound extensions") is something that we do need to support, as some file types do use that. For example things like .tar.gz. See also <!----></span>





issue 1136053



<a class="strike-through" target="_blank" href="/p/chromium/issues/detail?id=1136053" title="Save File Dialog with compound extensions"><!---->issue 1136053<!----></a>





 



<span class="line"><!----> <!----></span>





for some related issues to how compound extensions are treated.



<span class="line"><!---->for some related issues to how compound extensions are treated.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





One way to solve issues with misleading descriptions would be to completely ignore all descriptions in save dialogs, and only use auto-generated descriptions from the extensions. That wouldn't be great though since there are legit use cases for having multiple options for the same extension only differing in the description (for example chrome's save page as dialog has "Webpage, HTML only" and "Webpage, complete" options that both use the same (.htm) extension). Today that use case isn't supported since the API doesn't expose the selected option, but this still seems like a use case we don't want to preemptively rule out.



<span class="line"><!---->One way to solve issues with misleading descriptions would be to completely ignore all descriptions in save dialogs, and only use auto-generated descriptions from the extensions. That wouldn't be great though since there are legit use cases for having multiple options for the same extension only differing in the description (for example chrome's save page as dialog has "Webpage, HTML only" and "Webpage, complete" options that both use the same (.htm) extension). Today that use case isn't supported since the API doesn't expose the selected option, but this still seems like a use case we don't want to preemptively rule out.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





So perhaps better is to make sure the file dialog always shows the actual extension(s), regardless of the description shown. Exactly how that is done will probably depend a bit on the individual platform (although we could prepend the extensions to the description for example). There are a lot of differences already in how different platforms implement filters today. I think this will end up being a balance between fitting in with the platform and still giving enough information for users to make informed security decisions.



<span class="line"><!---->So perhaps better is to make sure the file dialog always shows the actual extension(s), regardless of the description shown. Exactly how that is done will probably depend a bit on the individual platform (although we could prepend the extensions to the description for example). There are a lot of differences already in how different platforms implement filters today. I think this will end up being a balance between fitting in with the platform and still giving enough information for users to make informed security decisions.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





My plan is to figure out exactly what we're doing today on all the various platforms (and possibly even various settings on those platforms), and then come up with some proposal to run by UX and security.



<span class="line"><!---->My plan is to figure out exactly what we're doing today on all the various platforms (and possibly even various settings on those platforms), and then come up with some proposal to run by UX and security.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





+pwnall for visibilty



<span class="line"><!---->+pwnall for visibilty<!----></span>



<br>





+asully since there is some overlap between this issue and allowing websites to provide a suggested filename as well



<span class="line"><!---->+asully since there is some overlap between this issue and allowing websites to provide a suggested filename as well<!----></span>

Misleading descriptions - How about creating a whitelist of chars in descriptions? Like "aA-zZ 0-9 , " + maximum 30 length? Because of that, the developer cannot add chars like "( ) . *" But this will block localization/globalization chars from other languages example: ł ó ż ź ć € ä ö ü and more... 



<span class="line"><!---->Misleading descriptions - How about creating a whitelist of chars in descriptions? Like "aA-zZ 0-9 , " + maximum 30 length? Looking into this one a bit more, you don't actually need any of the spaces to hide the real extension in the windows file dialog. Merely including (*.jpeg) in the description appears to be enough to have the system not include the real extensions. The space trick also works if you want a filter that doesn't show extensions at all.



<span class="line"><!---->Looking into this one a bit more, you don't actually need any of the spaces to hide the real extension in the windows file dialog. Merely including (*.jpeg) in the description appears to be enough to have the system not include the real extensions. The space trick also works if you want a filter that doesn't show extensions at all.<!----></span>

. As I mentioned there are two methods to hide real extensions:



<span class="line"><!---->. As I mentioned there are two methods to hide real extensions:<!----></span>



<br>





1) By many space characters (hide real extensions)



<span class="line"><!---->1) By many space characters (hide real extensions)<!----></span>



<br>





2) By *. characters (real extensions disappears) (picture40.png)



<span class="line"><!---->2) By *. characters (real extensions disappears) (picture40.png)<!----></span>

<span class="line"><!---->Date: Fri Dec 04 13:44:29 2020<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Add restrictions to allowed extensions for File System Access API



<span class="line"><!---->Add restrictions to allowed extensions for File System Access API<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





These restrictions apply to showOpenFilePicker and showSaveFilePicker.



<span class="line"><!---->These restrictions apply to showOpenFilePicker and showSaveFilePicker.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Existing restriction:



<span class="line"><!---->Existing restriction:<!----></span>



<br>





- Extension must start with "."



<span class="line"><!---->- Extension must start with "."<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





New restrictions:



<span class="line"><!---->New restrictions:<!----></span>



<br>





- Allowed code points: [A-Za-z0-9+.]



<span class="line"><!---->- Allowed code points: [A-Za-z0-9+.]<!----></span>



<br>





- Extension length cannot exceed to 16, inclusive of leading "."



<span class="line"><!---->- Extension length cannot exceed to 16, inclusive of leading "."<!----></span>



<br>





- Extension cannot end with "."



<span class="line"><!---->- Extension cannot end with "."<!----></span>



<br>





- Extension cannot end with "local" or "lnk"



<span class="line"><!---->- Extension cannot end with "local" or "lnk"<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Bug: 1137247



<a class="strike-through" target="_blank" href="/p/chromium/issues/detail?id=1137247" title="Security: Spoofing download filename extension in 86 chrome - showSaveFilePicker"><!---->Bug: 1137247<!----></a>





, 



<span class="line"><!---->, <!----></span>





1140410



<a class="strike-through" target="_blank" href="/p/chromium/issues/detail?id=1140410" title="Security:  Hide real extension of file by RTL - showSaveFilePicker"><!---->1140410<!----></a>





, 



<span class="line"><!---->, <!----></span>





1140417



<a class="strike-through" target="_blank" href="/p/chromium/issues/detail?id=1140417" title="Security: showSaveFilePicker allowing to save .lnk and .local files on windows!"><!---->1140417<!----></a>





,

Add restrictions to allowed extensions for File System Access API



<span class="line"><!---->Add restrictions to allowed extensions for File System Access API<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





These restrictions apply to showOpenFilePicker and showSaveFilePicker.



<span class="line"><!---->These restrictions apply to showOpenFilePicker and showSaveFilePicker.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Existing restriction:



<span class="line"><!---->Existing restriction:<!----></span>



<br>





- Extension must start with "."



<span class="line"><!---->- Extension must start with "."<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





New restrictions:



<span class="line"><!---->New restrictions:<!----></span>



<br>





- Allowed code points: [A-Za-z0-9+.]



<span class="line"><!---->- Allowed code points: [A-Za-z0-9+.]<!----></span>



<br>





- Extension length cannot exceed to 16, inclusive of leading "."



<span class="line"><!---->- Extension length cannot exceed to 16, inclusive of leading "."<!----></span>



<br>





- Extension cannot end with "."



<span class="line"><!---->- Extension cannot end with "."<!----></span>



<br>





- Extension cannot end with "local" or "lnk"



<span class="line"><!---->- Extension cannot end with "local" or "lnk"<!----></span>



<br>



<br>

<span class="line"><!---->(cherry picked from commit <!----></span>

Let me just make a point that the bug is a serious high-security problem.



<span class="line"><!---->Let me just make a point that the bug is a serious high-security problem.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





If a user sees the OS/Chrome download dialog [pic1.png], he is 100% sure that he can trust it because the window is not a part of the website, it is a part of the Operating System. I can respect that the description should be editable, I agree with that. However, right now it is allowed to trick users to download a dangerous file.



<span class="line"><!---->If a user sees the OS/Chrome download dialog [pic1.png], he is 100% sure that he can trust it because the window is not a part of the website, it is a part of the Operating System. I can respect that the description should be editable, I agree with that. However, right now it is allowed to trick users to download a dangerous file.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





In the video case, the user sees “JPEG Image (*.jpg)”, therefore the user is 100% sure that he can download and run it. Most users don't double-check to recognize if a file has the right extension, especially if the downloading file is an image .JPG that cannot be a virus.



<span class="line"><!---->In the video case, the user sees “JPEG Image (*.jpg)”, therefore the user is 100% sure that he can download and run it. Most users don't double-check to recognize if a file has the right extension, especially if the downloading file is an image .JPG that cannot be a virus.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The method is great for ransomware spreading, remote administration tools, and spreading other viruses. It will increase the open success rate by victims. Obviously, the bug is not an RCE, indeed is a security bug.



<span class="line"><!---->The method is great for ransomware spreading, remote administration tools, and spreading other viruses. It will increase the open success rate by victims. Obviously, the bug is not an RCE, indeed is a security bug.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Why just not use the simplest way to solve the problem?



<span class="line"><!---->Why just not use the simplest way to solve the problem?<!----></span>



<br>





Block * character in the description and limit characters length?



<span class="line"><!---->Block * character in the description and limit characters length?<!----></span>

characters, and on windows strips out '*' characters to ensure the

windows dialog itself will still include the true extension.

*** Boilerplate reminders! ***



<span class="line"><!---->*** Boilerplate reminders! ***<!----></span>



<br>





Please do NOT publicly disclose details until a fix has been released to all our users. Early public disclosure may cancel the provisional reward. Also, please be considerate about disclosure when the bug affects a core library that may be used by other products. Please do NOT share this information with third parties who are not directly involved in fixing the bug. Doing so may cancel the provisional reward. Please be honest if you have already disclosed anything publicly or to third parties. Lastly, we understand that some of you are not interested in money. We offer the option to donate your reward to an eligible charity. If you prefer this option, let us know and we will also match your donation - subject to our discretion. Any rewards that are unclaimed after 12 months will be donated to a charity of our choosing.



<span class="line"><!---->Please do NOT publicly disclose details until a fix has been released to all our users. Early public disclosure may cancel the provisional reward. Any rewards that are unclaimed after 12 months will be donated to a charity of our choosing.<!----></span>

Hi,



<span class="line"><!---->Hi,<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





File extension still can be hidden if user has unchecked "File name extension" in File explorer on Windows. By default the option is UNCHECKED.



<span class="line"><!---->File extension still can be hidden if user has unchecked "File name extension" in File explorer on Windows. By default the option is UNCHECKED.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Example: 



<span class="line"><!---->Example: <!----></span>





https://pulik.io/msexploit/Dynamics365web.pdf



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://pulik.io/msexploit/Dynamics365web.pdf"><!---->https://pulik.io/msexploit/Dynamics365web.pdf<!----></a>



<br>



<br>





For a better view of the problem, I have created an example - PDF Reader with the exploit. Below we can read an example use case.



<span class="line"><!---->For a better view of the problem, I have created an example - PDF Reader with the exploit. Below we can read an example use case.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The user read a pdf file, but after 3 seconds he gets a pop-up to encourage him to download a file. The user downloads the file because he knows that pdf is a safe file, he runs a downloaded file and gets infected by ransomware. (in example .bat runs only calculator)



<span class="line"><!---->The user read a pdf file, but after 3 seconds he gets a pop-up to encourage him to download a file. The user downloads the file because he knows that pdf is a safe file, he runs a downloaded file and gets infected by ransomware. (in example .bat runs only calculator)<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Someone first reported that here: 



<span class="line"><!---->Someone first reported that here: <!----></span>





https://bugs.chromium.org/p/chromium/issues/detail?id=1208439



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://bugs.chromium.org/p/chromium/issues/detail?id=1208439"><!---->https://bugs.chromium.org/p/chromium/issues/detail?id=1208439<!----></a>



<br>



<br>





The bug works on production in Google Chrome, Microsoft Edge and Opera



<span class="line"><!---->The bug works on production in Google Chrome, Microsoft Edge and Opera<!----></span>
